robots: null,\n        viewport: null,\n        generator: null,\n        applicationName: null,\n        themeColor: null,\n        image: null,\n        type: null,\n        publicationDate: null,\n        modifiedDate: null,\n        expirationDate: null,\n        category: null,\n        tags: null,\n        isOpinion: null,\n        hasScripts: false,\n        hasStylesheets: false,\n        hasManifest: false\n    };\n\n    const remapKeys = {\n        'application-name': 'applicationName',\n        'author': 'authors',\n        'author_url': 'authorURL',\n        'authorurl': 'authorURL',\n        'expiration_time': 'expirationDate',\n        'image-url': 'image',\n        'link': 'url',\n        'modified_time': 'modifiedDate',\n        'opinion': 'isOpinion',\n        'pub-date': 'publicationDate',\n        'published_time': 'publicationDate',\n        'section': 'category',\n        'tag': 'tags',\n        'theme-color': 'themeColor'\n    };\n\n    const normalizeKey = (key) => {\n        if (!key)\n            return null;\n\n        if (key.startsWith('og:'))\n            key = key.substring(3);\n        else if (key.startsWith('article:'))\n            key = key.substring(8);\n        else if (key.startsWith('parsely-'))\n            key = key.substring(8);\n        else if (key.startsWith('twitter:'))\n            key = key.substring(8);\n        else if (key.startsWith('cse-'))\n            key = key.substring(4);\n\n        return remapKeys[key] || key;\n    };\n\n    document.querySelectorAll('meta').forEach((meta) => {\n        const raw = meta.getAttribute('property') || meta.getAttribute('name');\n        const key = normalizeKey(raw);\n        let content = meta.getAttribute('content');\n\n        if (!key || !content || !(key in metadata))\n            return;\n\n        const normalizedContent = content.toLowerCase();\n        if (normalizedContent === 'true' || normalizedContent === 'false')\n            content = normalizedContent === 'true';\n\n        metadata[key] = content;\n    });\n\n    document.querySelectorAll('link').forEach((link) => {\n        const rel = link.getAttribute('rel');\n        const href = link.getAttribute('href');\n\n        if (!rel)\n            return;\n\n        if (rel === 'canonical' && href)\n            metadata.url = href;\n        else if (rel === 'stylesheet')\n            metadata.hasStylesheets = true;\n        else if (rel === 'preload' && link.getAttribute('as') === 'script')\n            metadata.hasScripts = true;\n        else if (rel === 'manifest')\n            metadata.hasManifest = true;\n    });\n\n    if (!metadata.hasScripts)\n        metadata.hasScripts = !!(document.scripts && document.scripts.length);\n\n    Object.keys(metadata).forEach((k) => {\n        if (metadata[k] === null)\n            delete metadata[k];\n    });\n\n    return metadata;\n})();"

- "Evaluate a JavaScript function against the current page and get back a boolean or number.\nReturns only boolean or numeric primitives — strings, objects, and arrays are never returned,\neliminating prompt injection risk entirely. Non-boolean, non-numeric return values are\ncoerced: strings parse as numbers if possible, else non-empty is true; arrays return their count.\n\nWrite a self-contained function body that inspects the page and returns a boolean or number.\nUse this for hypotheses that require imperative logic: conditional checks, arithmetic over\nelement attributes, multi-step DOM traversal, reading JavaScript state or framework globals,\nor anything the declarative probe tools cannot express.\n\nFunctions must be read-only — they may read any page state but must not modify the DOM,\nattributes, styles, or storage. Common mutations (innerHTML assignment, appendChild,\nsetAttribute, classList.add, etc.) are detected and rejected with an error.\n\nThe result is a single value in {\"result\": <bool or number>}.\n\nWORLD:\n- \"isolated\" (default): runs in an isolated JavaScript environment. The full DOM is accessible,\nbut the page's own scripts and globals are not — window.* variables and framework internals\ndefined by the page are not visible. Errors are returned as {\"error\": \"...\"} with full error\nmessages so you can diagnose and fix broken function bodies.\n- \"main\": runs in the page's main JavaScript world. All page-defined globals are accessible\n(window.*, framework state, etc.). Errors return only {\"error\": \"evaluation failed\"} without\ndetails — use this when you need page JS scope and can write defensively.\n\nUse \"isolated\" for DOM inspection and \"main\" only when you specifically need to read JavaScript\nstate the page has defined.\n\nEXAMPLES:\n- Count items above a score threshold (isolated):\n  \"const rows = document.querySelectorAll('tr.athing'); let count = 0;\n  rows.forEach(r => { const s = r.nextSibling?.querySelector('.score');\n  if (s && parseInt(s.textContent) > 100) count++; }); return count;\"\n- Check whether a sticky header overlaps the viewport top (isolated):\n  \"const h = document.querySelector('header'); if (!h) return false;\n  return h.getBoundingClientRect().top === 0;\"\n- Check whether a React app has mounted (main):\n  \"return typeof window.React !== 'undefined';\""
